Caption: The brightly-coloured waxcaps are often thought of as the orchids of the fungi kingdom because they are so vibrant and showy, and also quite particular. They will only grow on undisturbed, nutrient-poor grasslands like ancient pasture and other land that has never been ploughed or fertilised. As a result, many species are rare and hard to find but some grow much closer to home â€“ literally. Waxcaps can appear in garden lawns, grassy churchyards and even the occasional cricket pitch as long as the conditions are right. Wherever you find them, their presence means youâ€™re in a very special place. Labels: Smile Wool Woolen Happiness Food Dessert
Caption: In 2004 I was cultivating Reishi in Chile, studying from the only books available to me. I saved up, packed the essential, & took off to take @paulstamets course on cultivating gourmet and medicinal mushrooms. He was the author of those books, and the course was taught by him at @fungiperfecti in the PNW. It was incredible! Paul (who was still heavily stammering, btw @fantasticfungi) taught with passion and intense knowledge. This is where I first met somebody who loved fungi as much as I did. A brother. It truly was an awakening for me to understand that it was ok to be mushroom mad like Paul. I learnt to cultivate lion's mane (in the photo), shiitake, oysters, and more. Was taught how to make plug spawn, grain spawn, liquid spawn. I will never forget this transformational trip during my self-learning path in mycology. If a young woman from Chile did this in the late 90's/early 2000's, you all can do it now! Shout out to my awesome classmates @bigsilly49 @postcodeman @dameinpack @traddcotter #dontstop #thinkfungi #fungiaretheforce #mushrooms #thefutureisfungi #hongos #mycelium #micelio #rotnmould #rotnmold

Caption: We must not continue down this path of indiscriminate war on microbes. ğŸ”¬ The soil microbes, and the beneficial microbes of our body, are the foundation of all life. In our misunderstanding and fear of specific microbes, we have launched an all out war on Nature. Bacteria, fungi, and viruses are critical to life on Earth. Antibiotics, pesticides and fungicides, sanitizers, etc are being used so injudiciously, that the very fabric of human and planetary health is at stake. We must learn the patience to discover the difference between friend and foe. As with all things in Nature, diversity is the key. Without diversity, the system collapses. The invisible microbes do not have a voice of their own - at least not in the traditional sense. But if we continue to ignore them, the microbial ecosystem will become so imbalanced that we will be forced to pay attention to their power. There is no life in a fully sterilized world. We must learn to live alongside these microbes, and acknowledge the significant role they play in the health of our planet. #microbes #invisible #tiny #microscopic #soilorganisms #organism #life #earth #motherearth #ecosystem #circleoflife #systemsthinking #systems #fungicides #pesticides

Caption: "Magic Mushroom Cultivationâ€ by Steven Pollock M.D. (1977) is one of the legendary texts in the cultivation of "magic mushrooms". Many popular books were published in the US during the 70â€™s about the cultivation of Psilocybe spp., but this one stands out as one of the better known, particularly because in time Pollock was (incorrectly) associated with the cubensis strain "P envy". Pollock is also well known for finding and cultivating P. tampanensis, aka "Philosophers Stones". Psilocybe cubensis is one of the most cultivated mushrooms, and as a consequence of extensive collection, cultivation, breeding, and marketing ploys by various spore print sellers numerous â€œstrainsâ€ now exist. Unfortunately, much of the history of many of the older strains has been lost, or exist within obfuscated narratives from a variety of websites, with the person/s responsible having disappeared into history. Cailleux and Heim were the first to grow cultures of P. cubensis (as Stropharia cubensis), publishing their methods in 1957. During the late 1960â€™s and early 1970â€™s, those with access to scientific literature adapted laboratory techniques for the cultivation of Psilocybe spp., notably R.E. Brown and associates who published â€œThe Psychedelic Guide to the Preparation of the Eucharist in a Few of Its Many Guisesâ€ which was the first countercultural text to mention the cultivation of P. cubensis. Caption: "Magic Mushroom Cultivationâ€ by Steven Pollock M.D. (1977) is one of the legendary texts in the cultivation of "magic mushrooms". Many popular books were published in the US during the 70â€™s about the cultivation of Psilocybe spp., but this one stands out as one of the better known, particularly because in time Pollock was (incorrectly) associated with the cubensis strain "P envy". Pollock is also well known for finding and cultivating P. tampanensis, aka "Philosophers Stones". Psilocybe cubensis is one of the most cultivated mushrooms, and as a consequence of extensive collection, cultivation, breeding, and marketing ploys by various spore print sellers numerous â€œstrainsâ€ now exist. Unfortunately, much of the history of many of the older strains has been lost, or exist within obfuscated narratives from a variety of websites, with the person/s responsible having disappeared into history. Cailleux and Heim were the first to grow cultures of P. cubensis (as Stropharia cubensis), publishing their methods in 1957. During the late 1960â€™s and early 1970â€™s, those with access to scientific literature adapted laboratory techniques for the cultivation of Psilocybe spp., notably R.E. Brown and associates who published â€œThe Psychedelic Guide to the Preparation of the Eucharist in a Few of Its Many Guisesâ€ which was the first countercultural text to mention the cultivation of P. cubensis. Other books include â€œGrowing Wild Mushroomsâ€ by Harris (1976), â€œPsilocybin: Magic Mushroom Grower's Guideâ€ by Oss & Oeric (1976), â€œHow to Identify and Grow Psilocybin Mushroomsâ€ by Gutierrez & Stevens (1977), â€œTeonanÃ¡catl : hallucinogenic mushrooms of North Americaâ€ by Ott & Bigwood (1978), and â€œThe mushroom Cultivatorâ€ by Stamets and Chilton(1983) #guerrillamycology #ğŸ„ #thinkfungi #fungi #funghi #fungus #hongos #mushrooms #mycology #mycophile #mycophilia #fungicultureÂ  #fungifanatic #mycelium #myceliumrunning #ethnomycology #radicalmycology #hallucinogenicfungi #hallucinogenic #entheogens #rogerheim #pollock #stevenpollock #magicmushroomcultivation #psilocybe #psilocybecubensis #psychedelicliterautre #penvy #philosophersstones #mushroomcultivation

Post ID: 2499136695720894185
Date: 2021-02-01 00:45:31
Labels: Petal Pink Font Rose family Flower Arranging Floristry Cut flowers Garden roses Floral design Rose
Caption: You might have read our recent post about the excessive use of damaging pesticides in imported cut flowers, but of almost equal concern is fungicide usage. You see, Ecuador, where many of the roses sold in the US are grown, has high amounts of rainfall and the greenhouses where these flowers are grown are notorious for holding in humidity and creating fungus issues like Botrytis. Botrytis can create spots on a rose, and often won't appear on a rose until after it's left the farm. To prevent these spots from showing up on roses once they hit the retail market and dissuading customers from buying them, foreign growers have developed a worrisome and toxic method of dipping the entire rose into a vat of fungicide, first dunking the bloom, and then the stem. The workers in charge of this job wear respirator masks to avoid inhaling the products, which are then packaged directly into flower sleeves and shipped to the US (no, they are not rinsed off afterward). Of the 37 products that are used as rose dip treatments, 17 of them have been identified by the Pesticide Action Network to be problematic as groundwater pollutants or harmful to humans, toxic to life and the environment. Unfortunately, Valentine's Day, the biggest flower holiday in the US, is also a time when domestic roses are, by and large, dormant in their fields. This means the VAST majority of cut roses purchased during February have been dipped in a toxic blend of fungicides and pesticides. Not exactly the way I'd want to say "I love you!" #flowers #colorado #coloradoflorist #farmerflorist #coloradofarmer #localflowers #pesticides #fungicides #toxicflowers #valentinesdayflowers #valentinesday #denver #denverflorist #roses #importedroses #buyamericangrown #americangrown #supportlocalflowers #supportamericanfarms #buyamericangrown #coloradogrown #freshcutcolorado #coloradoflowers
